                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">حَبٌّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حب</orth>
                  </form>, (S, Msb, K,) a [coll.] gen. n., (Msb,) n. un. <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّةٌ</foreign>; (S, Msb, K;) <hi rend="ital">Grain</hi> of wheat, barley, lentils, rice, &amp;c.: (Az, TA:) accord. to Ks, only of wheat and barley: (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">wheat &amp;c. while in the ears</hi> or <hi rend="ital">other envelopes:</hi> (Msb:) [but applied also to various other <hi rend="ital">seeds;</hi> among which, to beans, (as in the Mgh in art. <foreign lang="ar">بقل</foreign>,) and peas and the like; and <hi rend="ital">kernels;</hi> and] the <hi rend="ital">stones</hi> of grapes, dates, pomegranates, and the like: (Mgh voce <foreign lang="ar">عجَمٌ</foreign>:) by some it is applied even [to <hi rend="ital">berries;</hi> as, for instance,] to <hi rend="ital">grapes:</hi> you say <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّةٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ عِنَبٍ</foreign>, as well as <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ البُرِّ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ الشَّعِيرِ</foreign>, and the like: (TA:) [and hence, to <hi rend="ital">beads:</hi> (see <foreign lang="ar">حِبٌّ</foreign>:)] the pl. (of <foreign lang="ar">حَبٌّ</foreign>, Msb) is <foreign lang="ar">حُبُوبٌ</foreign> (S, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">حُبَّانٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">تُمْرَانٌ</foreign>, (K,) pl. of <foreign lang="ar">تَمْرٌ</foreign>; (TA;) and (of <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّةٌ</foreign>, Msb) <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّاتٌ</foreign> (Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">حِبَابٌ</foreign>, [or this is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">حَبٌّ</foreign> also,] like <foreign lang="ar">كِلَابٌ</foreign> as pl. of <foreign lang="ar">كَلْبَةٌ</foreign> [and of <foreign lang="ar">كَلْبٌ</foreign>]: (Msb:) and <foreign lang="ar">حَبٌّ</foreign> is also called [by lexicologists, but not by grammarians,] a pl. of <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّةٌ</foreign>.                   <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">حُبٌّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حب</orth>
                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Love; affection;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">وُدٌّ</foreign>, (A,) or <foreign lang="ar">وِدَادٌ</foreign>; (K;) <hi rend="ital">inclination of the nature,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">natural disposition, towards a thing that pleases,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">delights;</hi> (Kull p. 165;) <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بُغْضٌ</foreign>: (Mgh, TA:) <foreign lang="ar">حُبٌّ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n6847-1" target="حِبٌّ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n6848"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n6847-2" target="حُبَّةٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n6850"/></foreign> [this being said in the S to be syn. with <foreign lang="ar">حُبٌّ</foreign> and in the K to be syn. with <foreign lang="ar">مَحَبَّةٌ</foreign>, and it is used as an inf. n. in an ex. cited voce <foreign lang="ar">دَاحٌ</foreign> in art. <foreign lang="ar">دوح</foreign>,] and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n6847-3" target="حُبَابٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n6855"/></foreign> (S, K) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n6847-4" target="حِبَابٌ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n6856"/></foreign> (K) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n6847-5" target="مَحَبَّةٌ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n6864"/></foreign> (S) signify the same; (S, K;) i. e., as above. (K.) The degrees of <foreign lang="ar">حُبّ</foreign> are as follow: first, <foreign lang="ar">هَوًى</foreign>, the “ inclining of the soul, or mind; ” also applied to the “ object of love itself: ” then, <foreign lang="ar">عَلَاقَةٌ</foreign>, “ love cleaving to the heart; ” so termed because of the heart's cleaving to the object of love: then, <foreign lang="ar">كَلَفٌ</foreign>, “ violent, or intense, love; ” from <foreign lang="ar">كُلْفَةٌ</foreign> signifying “ difficulty, or distress, or affliction: ” then, <foreign lang="ar">عِشْقٌ</foreign>, [“ amorous desire; ” or “ passionate love; ”] in the S, “ excess of love; ” and in the language of the physicians, “ a kind of melancholy: ” then, <foreign lang="ar">شَغَفٌ</foreign>, “ ardour of love, accompanied by a sensation of pleasure; ” like <foreign lang="ar">لَوْعَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لَاعِجٌ</foreign>; the former of which is “ ardour of love; ” and the latter, “ ardent love: ” then, <foreign lang="ar">جَوًى</foreign>, “ inward love; ” and “ violence of amorous desire, ” or “ of grief, or sorrow: ” then, <foreign lang="ar">تَتَيُّمٌ</foreign>, “ a state of enslavement by love: ” then <foreign lang="ar">تَبْلٌ</foreign>, “ lovesickness: ” then, <foreign lang="ar">وَلَهٌ</foreign>, “ distraction, or loss of reason, in love: ” and then, <foreign lang="ar">هُيَامٌ</foreign> “ a state of wandering about at random in consequence of overpowering love. ” (Kull ubi suprà.) [Accord. to the Msb, it is a simple subst.: but accord. to the K, an inf. n.; and hence,] <foreign lang="ar">حُبًّا لِمَا أَحْبَبْتُمْ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">أُحِبُّ حُبًّا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I love with loving,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">much, what ye have loved</hi>]. (Har p. 186.) Hence the phrase, <foreign lang="ar">نَعَمْ <ref cref="n6847-6" target="وَحُبَّةً" n="6" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>وَكَرَامَةً</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Yea; and with love and honour</hi> will I do what thou requirest: or <hi rend="ital">for the sake of</hi> the <hi rend="ital">love and honour</hi> that I bear thee: or <foreign lang="ar">حبّة</foreign> may be here used for <foreign lang="ar">حُبًّا</foreign> to assimilate it in termination to <foreign lang="ar">كرامة</foreign>: see what follows]. (S, TA.) Hence also the saying of Abu-l-' Atà EsSindee, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">فَوَٱللّٰهِ مَا أَدْرِى وَإِنِّى لَصَادِقٌ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَدَآءٌ عَرَانِى مِنْ حُبَابِكِ أَمْ سِحْرُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And by God, I know not</hi> (<hi rend="ital">and indeed I am speaking truth</hi>) <hi rend="ital">whether disease have befallen me in consequence of love of thee, or enchantment</hi>]: (S, TA:) but IB says that the reading best known is   
      <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ <ref cref="n6847-7" target="حِبَابِكِ" n="7" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; and that <foreign lang="ar">حِباب</foreign>, here, may be an inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">حَابَبْتُهُ</foreign>; or it may be pl. of <foreign lang="ar">حُبٌّ</foreign>, like as <foreign lang="ar">عِشاشٌ</foreign> is of <foreign lang="ar">عُشٌّ</foreign>; (TA;) or it may be an inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">حَبَبْتُهُ</foreign>: some also read

                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حباحب</orth>
                  </form>, (K,) or <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو حُبَاحِبٍ</foreign>, (S,) [<hi rend="ital">A kind of fire-fly;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a fly that flies in the night,</hi> (K,) <hi rend="ital">resembling fire,</hi> (S,) <hi rend="ital">emitting rays like a lamp:</hi> (K:) AHn says that <foreign lang="ar">حباحب</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ابوحباحب</foreign> were both unknown to him, and that nothing respecting them had been heard by him from the Arabs; but that some people asserted the insect thus called to be the <foreign lang="ar">يَرَاع</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">a moth that, when it flies by night, no person not knowing it would doubt to be a spark of fire:</hi> Aboo-Tálib says, as on the authority of Arabs of the desert, that <foreign lang="ar">حباحب</foreign> is the name of a <hi rend="ital">flying thing longer than the common fly, and slender, that flies between sunset and nightfall, resembling a spark of fire:</hi> (TA:) or, accord. to As, it is <hi rend="ital">a flying thing, like the common fly, with a wing that becomes red; when it flies appearing at a distance like a lighted piece of fire-wood.</hi> (Har p. 500.) <foreign lang="ar">نَارُ الحُبَاحِبِ</foreign> (S, K) and <foreign lang="ar">نَارُأَبِى حُبَاحِبٍ</foreign> and simply <foreign lang="ar">الحُبَاحِبُ</foreign> (S) mean <hi rend="ital">The fire of the fly above mentioned:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of El-Hobáhib</hi> or <hi rend="ital">Aboo-Hobáhib:</hi> (TA:) [for] El-Hobáhib, (S,) or Aboo-Hobáhib, (K,) is said to have been a niggardly man, who never lighted any but a faint fire, fearing to attract guests, so that his fire became proverbial. (S, K.) El-Kumeyt says, describing swords, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">يَرَى الرَّاؤُونَ بِالشَّفَرَاتِ مِنْهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">كَنَارِ أَبِى حُبَاحِبَ وَالظُّبِينَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> 
                  <pb n="498"/> [<hi rend="ital">The beholders see, in the sides of the blades thereof, and the extremities, the semblance of the fire of the fire-fly</hi>]: (S:) here the poet has made <foreign lang="ar">حباحب</foreign> imperfectly decl., regarding it as a fem. [proper] name [of the fly above mentioned]. (TA.) Or <foreign lang="ar">نارالحباحب</foreign> (S, K) and simply <foreign lang="ar">الحباحب</foreign> (S) signify <hi rend="ital">The fire that is struck by a horse's hoofs:</hi> (Fr, S:) or <hi rend="ital">the sparks of fire that are made to fly forth in the air by the collision of stones:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the sparks that fall from the pieces of wood that are used for producing fire</hi> [<hi rend="ital">by means of friction</hi>]: (K:) or they are derived from <foreign lang="ar">حَبْحَبَةٌ</foreign>, (IAar, K,) signifying “ weakness, ” (IAar, TA,) [and their meaning is <hi rend="ital">faint fire.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أُمُّ حُبَاحِبٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A flying insect resembling the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">species of locust called</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">جُنْدَب</foreign>, (K, * TA,) <hi rend="ital">spotted with yellow and green:</hi> when people see it, they say, <foreign lang="ar">بَرِّدِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَا حُبَاحِبُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Spread forth thy wings</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">بُرْدَيْكِ</foreign>), <hi rend="ital">hobáhib</hi>]; whereupon it spreads its two wings, which are adorned with red and yellow. (TA.)    </entryFree>35:T109c,<entryFree id="n6859" key="حَبَّذَا" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">حَبَّذَا</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">حَبِيبٌ</foreign>, as in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّذَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَمْرُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Loved, beloved, affected, loved,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">approved, is the thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affair;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lovely, charming,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">excellent, is it</hi>]; (K;) and in <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّذَا زَيْدٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Loved, beloved,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">is Zeyd</hi>]; (S;) is composed <hi rend="ital">of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّ</foreign>, (Sb, Fr, S, K,) a verb of praise, in the pret. form, invariable, originally <foreign lang="ar">حَبُبَ</foreign>, (Fr, S,) and <foreign lang="ar">ذَا</foreign>, (Sb, Fr, S, K,) its agent, (S,) which together constitute it a single word, (Sb, S, K,) a noun, (Sb, K,) or occupying the place of a noun, (S,) governing the noun [particularized by praise] that follows it in the nom. case; (Sb, S, K;) the place that it occupies in construction making it virtually in the nom. case as an inchoative, and the noun that follows it being its enunciative: (S:) [but see what follows.] It is used in the same manner as a prov.; (Sb, K;) [i. e., it is not altered to agree in number or gender with the noun particularized by praise, which follows it;] remaining the same when used in the dual and pl. and fem. sense; so that one says, <foreign lang="ar">حبّذا زَيْدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الزَّيْدَانِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الزَّيْدُونَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">هِنْدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَنْتَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَنْتُمَا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَنْتُمْ</foreign> [&amp;c.]; (Ibn-Keysán, TA;) and <foreign lang="ar">حبّذا ٱمْرَأَةٌ</foreign>, not <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّذِهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المَرْأَةُ</foreign>; (Sb, S, K; *) which shows that the noun that follows it may not be regarded as a substitute for <foreign lang="ar">ذا</foreign>: (S:) [but see what follows.] It is allowable, but bad, to say, <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدٌ حَبَّذَا</foreign>. (TA.) [There are, however, various opinions respecting <foreign lang="ar">حبّذا</foreign> and the noun that follows it.] Some hold that <foreign lang="ar">حبّذا</foreign> is a noun, composed of <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ذا</foreign>, and is an inchoative, and that the noun particularized by praise is its enunciative; or that the former is an enunciative, and the latter an inchoative, reversing the usual order: others hold that <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّ</foreign> is a verb in the pret. form; and <foreign lang="ar">ذا</foreign>, its agent; and that the noun particularized by praise may be an inchoative, of which <foreign lang="ar">حبّذا</foreign> is the enunciative; or it may be an enunciative of which the inchoative is suppressed, so that <foreign lang="ar">حبّذا زَيْدٌ</foreign> is for <foreign lang="ar">حبّذا هُوَ زَيْدٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Loved,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beloved,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">is this</hi> person: <hi rend="ital">he is Zeyd</hi>], or <foreign lang="ar">حبّذا المَمْدُوحُ زَيْدٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">loved,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">is this</hi> person: <hi rend="ital">the</hi> person <hi rend="ital">praised is Zeyd</hi>]: others hold that <foreign lang="ar">حبّذا</foreign> is a pret. verb, composed of <foreign lang="ar">حَبَّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ذا</foreign>, and that the noun following it is its agent; but this is the weakest of opinions: one also says, in dispraise, <foreign lang="ar">لَاحَبَّذَا زَيْدٌ</foreign>.
